<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Beethoven_Waldmuller_1823.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="389" height="247" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Beethoven_Waldmuller_1823.jpg/200px-Beethoven_Waldmuller_1823.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Beethoven_Waldmuller_1823.jpg/300px-Beethoven_Waldmuller_1823.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/95/Beethoven_Waldmuller_1823.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Beethoven_Waldmuller_1823.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Beethoven in 1823 by Ferdinand Georg Waldmüller</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Beethoven then turned to writing the string quartets for Golitsin. This series of quartets, known as the "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Late_String_Quartets_(Beethoven)" title="Late String Quartets (Beethoven)">Late Quartets</a>," went far beyond what musicians or audiences were ready for at that time. One musician<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (December 2011)">who?</span></a></i>]</sup> commented that "we know there is something there, but we do not know what it is." Composer <a href="/wiki/Louis_Spohr" title="Louis Spohr">Louis Spohr</a> called them "indecipherable, uncorrected horrors." Opinion has changed considerably from the time of their first bewildered reception: their forms and ideas inspired musicians and composers including <a href="/wiki/Richard_Wagner" title="Richard Wagner">Richard Wagner</a> and <a href="/wiki/B%C3%A9la_Bart%C3%B3k" title="Béla Bartók">Béla Bartók</a>, and continue to do so. Of the late quartets, Beethoven's favourite was the <a href="/wiki/String_Quartet_No._14_(Beethoven)" title="String Quartet No. 14 (Beethoven)">Fourteenth Quartet, op. 131</a> in C<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;">♯</span> minor, which he rated as his most perfect single work.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morris2010_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-Morris2010-84">[84]</a></sup> The last musical wish of <a href="/wiki/Franz_Schubert" title="Franz Schubert">Schubert</a> was to hear the Op. 131 quartet, which he did on 14 November 1828, five days before his death.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Winter1994_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-Winter1994-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<p>Beethoven wrote the last quartets amidst failing health. In April 1825 he was bedridden, and remained ill for about a month. The illness—or more precisely, his recovery from it—is remembered for having given rise to the deeply felt slow movement of the <a href="/wiki/String_Quartet_No._15_(Beethoven)" title="String Quartet No. 15 (Beethoven)">Fifteenth Quartet</a>, which Beethoven called "Holy song of thanks ('Heiliger Dankgesang') to the divinity, from one made well." He went on to complete the quartets now numbered <a href="/wiki/String_Quartet_No._13_(Beethoven)" title="String Quartet No. 13 (Beethoven)">Thirteenth</a>, <a href="/wiki/String_Quartet_No._14_(Beethoven)" title="String Quartet No. 14 (Beethoven)">Fourteenth</a>, and <a href="/wiki/String_Quartet_No._16_(Beethoven)" title="String Quartet No. 16 (Beethoven)">Sixteenth</a>. The last work completed by Beethoven was the substitute final movement of the Thirteenth Quartet, which replaced the difficult <i><a href="/wiki/Gro%C3%9Fe_Fuge" title="Große Fuge">Große Fuge</a></i>. Shortly thereafter, in December 1826, illness struck again, with episodes of vomiting and diarrhoea that nearly ended his life.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In 1825, his nine symphonies were performed in a cycle for the first time, by the Leipzig Gewandhaus Orchestra under <a href="/wiki/Johann_Philipp_Christian_Schulz" title="Johann Philipp Christian Schulz">Johann Philipp Christian Schulz</a>. This was repeated in 1826.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Illness_and_death">Illness and death</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Ludwig_van_Beethoven" title="Death of Ludwig van Beethoven">Death of Ludwig van Beethoven</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Beethovendeathmask.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="362" height="235" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Beethovendeathmask.jpg/170px-Beethovendeathmask.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Beethovendeathmask.jpg/255px-Beethovendeathmask.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Beethovendeathmask.jpg/340px-Beethovendeathmask.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Beethovendeathmask.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Death mask by <a href="/wiki/Josef_Danhauser" title="Josef Danhauser">Josef Danhauser</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Zentralfriedhof_Vienna_-_Beethoven.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2560" data-file-width="1920" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Zentralfriedhof_Vienna_-_Beethoven.JPG/170px-Zentralfriedhof_Vienna_-_Beethoven.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Zentralfriedhof_Vienna_-_Beethoven.JPG/255px-Zentralfriedhof_Vienna_-_Beethoven.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Zentralfriedhof_Vienna_-_Beethoven.JPG/340px-Zentralfriedhof_Vienna_-_Beethoven.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Zentralfriedhof_Vienna_-_Beethoven.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Beethoven's grave site, Vienna <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zentralfriedhof" title="Zentralfriedhof">Zentralfriedhof</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Beethoven was bedridden for most of his remaining months, and many friends came to visit. He died on 26 March 1827 at the age of 56 during a thunderstorm. His friend <a href="/wiki/Anselm_H%C3%BCttenbrenner" title="Anselm Hüttenbrenner">Anselm Hüttenbrenner</a>, who was present at the time, said that there was a peal of thunder at the moment of death. An <a href="/wiki/Autopsy" title="Autopsy">autopsy</a> revealed significant <a href="/wiki/Liver" title="Liver">liver</a> damage, which may have been due to heavy alcohol consumption.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECooper2008318.2C_349_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECooper2008318.2C_349-88">[88]</a></sup> It also revealed considerable dilation of the auditory and other related nerves.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></p>
<p>Beethoven's funeral procession on 29 March 1827 was attended by an estimated 20,000 Viennese citizens. <a href="/wiki/Franz_Schubert" title="Franz Schubert">Franz Schubert</a>, who died the following year and was buried next to Beethoven, was one of the torchbearers. Beethoven was buried in a dedicated grave in the <a href="/wiki/W%C3%A4hring" title="Währing">Währing</a> cemetery, north-west of Vienna, after a requiem mass at the church of the Holy Trinity (Dreifaltigkeitskirche). His remains were <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exhume" title="Exhume">exhumed</a> for study in 1862, and moved in 1888 to Vienna's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zentralfriedhof" title="Zentralfriedhof">Zentralfriedhof</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECooper2008318.2C_349_88-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECooper2008318.2C_349-88">[88]</a></sup> In 2012, his crypt was checked to see if his teeth had been stolen during a series of grave robberies of other famous Viennese composers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<p>There is dispute about the cause of Beethoven's death: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alcoholic_cirrhosis" title="Alcoholic cirrhosis">alcoholic cirrhosis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Syphilis" title="Syphilis">syphilis</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Infectious_hepatitis" title="Infectious hepatitis">infectious hepatitis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lead_poisoning" title="Lead poisoning">lead poisoning</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sarcoidosis" title="Sarcoidosis">sarcoidosis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Whipple%27s_disease" title="Whipple's disease">Whipple's disease</a> have all been proposed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> Friends and visitors before and after his death clipped locks of his hair, some of which have been preserved and subjected to additional analysis, as have skull fragments removed during the 1862 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exhumation" title="Exhumation">exhumation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> Some of these analyses have led to controversial assertions that Beethoven was accidentally <a href="/wiki/Poison" title="Poison">poisoned</a> to death by excessive doses of lead-based treatments administered under instruction from his doctor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Beethoven_bust_statue_by_Hagen.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3500" data-file-width="2350" height="253" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Beethoven_bust_statue_by_Hagen.jpg/170px-Beethoven_bust_statue_by_Hagen.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Beethoven_bust_statue_by_Hagen.jpg/255px-Beethoven_bust_statue_by_Hagen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Beethoven_bust_statue_by_Hagen.jpg/340px-Beethoven_bust_statue_by_Hagen.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Beethoven_bust_statue_by_Hagen.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A bust by <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Hagen" title="Hugo Hagen">Hugo Hagen</a> based upon Beethoven's life mask</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Beethoven%27s_musical_style" title="Beethoven's musical style">Beethoven's musical style</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beethoven_and_C_minor" title="Beethoven and C minor">Beethoven and C minor</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_compositions_by_Ludwig_van_Beethoven" title="List of compositions by Ludwig van Beethoven">List of compositions by Ludwig van Beethoven</a></div>
<p>Beethoven is acknowledged to be one of the giants of <a href="/wiki/Classical_music" title="Classical music">classical music</a>. Together with <a href="/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach" title="Johann Sebastian Bach">Bach</a> and <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Brahms" title="Johannes Brahms">Brahms</a>, he is referred to as one of the "<a href="/wiki/Three_Bs" title="Three Bs">three <i>B</i>s</a>" who epitomize that tradition. He was a pivotal figure in the transition from the 18th century musical <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Classical_music_era" title="Classical music era">classicism</a> to 19th century <a href="/wiki/Romantic_music" title="Romantic music">romanticism</a>, and his influence on subsequent generations of composers was profound.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GroveOnline_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-GroveOnline-96">[96]</a></sup> His music features twice on the <a href="/wiki/Voyager_Golden_Record" title="Voyager Golden Record">Voyager Golden Record</a>, a phonograph record containing a broad sample of the images, common sounds, languages, and music of Earth, sent into outer space with the two <a href="/wiki/Voyager_program" title="Voyager program">Voyager</a> probes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Golden_Record_Music_List_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-Golden_Record_Music_List-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Overview">Overview</span></h3>
<p>Beethoven composed in several musical genres and for a variety of instrument combinations. His works for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Symphony_orchestra" title="Symphony orchestra">symphony orchestra</a> include nine <a href="/wiki/Symphony" title="Symphony">symphonies</a> (of which the Ninth Symphony includes a chorus), and about a dozen pieces of "occasional" music. He wrote seven <a href="/wiki/Concerto" title="Concerto">concerti</a> for one or more soloists and orchestra, as well as four shorter works that include soloists accompanied by orchestra. His only <a href="/wiki/Opera" title="Opera">opera</a> is <i><a href="/wiki/Fidelio" title="Fidelio">Fidelio</a></i>; other vocal works with orchestral accompaniment include two <a href="/wiki/Mass_(music)" title="Mass (music)">masses</a> and a number of shorter works.</p>
<p>His large body of compositions for <a href="/wiki/Piano" title="Piano">piano</a> includes 32 <a href="/wiki/Piano_sonata" title="Piano sonata">piano sonatas</a> and numerous shorter pieces, including arrangements of some of his other works. Works with piano accompaniment include 10 violin sonatas, 5 cello sonatas, and a sonata for <a href="/wiki/French_horn" title="French horn">French horn</a>, as well as numerous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lieder" title="Lieder">lieder</a>.</p>
<p>Beethoven also wrote a significant quantity of <a href="/wiki/Chamber_music" title="Chamber music">chamber music</a>. In addition to 16 <a href="/wiki/String_quartet" title="String quartet">string quartets</a>, he wrote five works for <a href="/wiki/String_quintet" title="String quintet">string quintet</a>, seven for <a href="/wiki/Piano_trio" title="Piano trio">piano trio</a>, five for <a href="/wiki/String_trio" title="String trio">string trio</a>, and more than a dozen works for various combinations of <a href="/wiki/Wind_instrument" title="Wind instrument">wind instruments</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_three_periods">The three periods</span></h3>
<p>Beethoven's compositional career is usually divided into early, middle, and late periods.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GroveOnline_96-1"><a href="#cite_note-GroveOnline-96">[96]</a></sup> In this scheme, his early period is taken to last until about 1802, the middle period from about 1803 to about 1814, and the late period from about 1815.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In his early period, Beethoven's work was strongly influenced by his predecessors <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Haydn" title="Joseph Haydn">Haydn</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart" title="Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart">Mozart</a>. He also explored new directions and gradually expanded the scope and ambition of his work. Some important pieces from the early period are the <a href="/wiki/Symphony_No._1_(Beethoven)" title="Symphony No. 1 (Beethoven)">first</a> and <a href="/wiki/Symphony_No._2_(Beethoven)" title="Symphony No. 2 (Beethoven)">second</a> symphonies, the set of six string quartets <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/String_Quartets_Nos._1%E2%80%936,_Op._18_(Beethoven)" title="String Quartets Nos. 1–6, Op. 18 (Beethoven)">Opus 18</a>, the first two piano concertos, and the first dozen or so <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beethoven%27s_piano_sonatas" title="Beethoven's piano sonatas">piano sonatas</a>, including the famous <i><a href="/wiki/Piano_Sonata_No._8_(Beethoven)" title="Piano Sonata No. 8 (Beethoven)">Pathétique</a></i> sonata, Op. 13.</p>
<p>His middle (heroic) period began shortly after Beethoven's personal crisis brought on by his recognition of encroaching deafness. It includes large-scale works that express heroism and struggle. Middle-period works include six symphonies (Nos. 3–8), the last three piano concertos, the <a href="/wiki/Triple_Concerto_(Beethoven)" title="Triple Concerto (Beethoven)">Triple Concerto</a> and <a href="/wiki/Violin_Concerto_(Beethoven)" title="Violin Concerto (Beethoven)">violin concerto</a>, five string quartets (Nos. 7–11), several piano sonatas (including the <i><a href="/wiki/Piano_Sonata_No._14_(Beethoven)" title="Piano Sonata No. 14 (Beethoven)">Moonlight</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Piano_Sonata_No._21_(Beethoven)" title="Piano Sonata No. 21 (Beethoven)">Waldstein</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Piano_Sonata_No._23_(Beethoven)" title="Piano Sonata No. 23 (Beethoven)">Appassionata</a></i> sonatas), the <i><a href="/wiki/Violin_Sonata_No._9_(Beethoven)" title="Violin Sonata No. 9 (Beethoven)">Kreutzer</a></i> violin sonata and Beethoven's only <a href="/wiki/Opera" title="Opera">opera</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Fidelio" title="Fidelio">Fidelio</a></i>.</p>
<p>Beethoven's late period began around 1815. Works from this period are characterised by their intellectual depth, their formal innovations, and their intense, highly personal expression. The <a href="/wiki/String_Quartet_No._14_(Beethoven)" title="String Quartet No. 14 (Beethoven)">String Quartet, Op. 131</a> has seven linked movements, and the <a href="/wiki/Symphony_No._9_(Beethoven)" title="Symphony No. 9 (Beethoven)">Ninth Symphony</a> adds choral forces to the orchestra in the last movement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GroveOnline_96-2"><a href="#cite_note-GroveOnline-96">[96]</a></sup> Other compositions from this period include the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Missa_Solemnis_(Beethoven)" title="Missa Solemnis (Beethoven)">Missa Solemnis</a></i>, the last five string quartets (including the massive <i><a href="/wiki/Gro%C3%9Fe_Fuge" title="Große Fuge">Große Fuge</a></i>) and the last five piano sonatas.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Character">Character</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Beethoven_walk.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="454" data-file-width="787" height="127" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Beethoven_walk.jpg/220px-Beethoven_walk.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Beethoven_walk.jpg/330px-Beethoven_walk.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Beethoven_walk.jpg/440px-Beethoven_walk.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Beethoven_walk.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Beethoven's walk in nature, <a href="/wiki/Julius_Schmid_(painter)" title="Julius Schmid (painter)">Julius Schmid</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Beethoven's personal life was troubled by his encroaching <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Post-lingual_hearing_impairment" title="Post-lingual hearing impairment">deafness</a> and irritability brought on by chronic abdominal pain (beginning in his twenties), which led him to contemplate suicide (documented in his <a href="/wiki/Heiligenstadt_Testament" title="Heiligenstadt Testament">Heiligenstadt Testament</a>). Beethoven was often irascible. It has been suggested he had <a href="/wiki/Bipolar_disorder" title="Bipolar disorder">bipolar disorder</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> Nevertheless, he had a close and devoted circle of friends all his life, thought to have been attracted by his strength of personality. Towards the end of his life, Beethoven's friends competed in their efforts to help him cope with his incapacities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GroveOnline_96-3"><a href="#cite_note-GroveOnline-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
<p>Sources show Beethoven's disdain for authority and for social rank. He stopped performing at the piano if the audience chatted amongst themselves, or afforded him less than their full attention. At soirées, he refused to perform if suddenly called upon to do so. Eventually, after many confrontations, the Archduke Rudolph decreed that the usual rules of court etiquette did not apply to Beethoven.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GroveOnline_96-4"><a href="#cite_note-GroveOnline-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
<p>Beethoven was attracted to the ideals of the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Enlightenment" title="Age of Enlightenment">Age of Enlightenment</a>. In 1804, when Napoleon's imperial ambitions became clear, Beethoven took hold of the title page of his <a href="/wiki/Symphony_No._3_(Beethoven)" title="Symphony No. 3 (Beethoven)">Third Symphony</a> and scratched the name Bonaparte out so violently that he made a hole in the paper. He later changed the work's title to "Sinfonia Eroica, composta per festeggiare il sovvenire d'un grand'uom" ("Heroic Symphony, composed to celebrate the memory of a great man"), and he rededicated it to his patron, Prince Joseph Franz von Lobkowitz, at whose palace it was first performed.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The fourth movement of his <a href="/wiki/Symphony_No._9_(Beethoven)" title="Symphony No. 9 (Beethoven)">Ninth Symphony</a> features an elaborate choral setting of <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Schiller" title="Friedrich Schiller">Schiller's</a> Ode <i><a href="/wiki/Ode_to_Joy" title="Ode to Joy">An die Freude</a></i> ("Ode to Joy"), an optimistic hymn championing the brotherhood of humanity.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_culture">In popular culture</span></h2>
<p>Beethoven has been the subject of a number of biographical films; see <a href="/wiki/Beethoven_in_film" title="Beethoven in film">Beethoven in film</a>.</p>
<p><i>Beethoven's Tenth</i> is a play in two acts by actor <a href="/wiki/Peter_Ustinov" title="Peter Ustinov">Peter Ustinov</a>. The first performances in the US were between 7 October and 27 November 1983, with Ustinov himself playing the leading role and supporting actors including <a href="/wiki/George_Rose_(actor)" title="George Rose (actor)">George Rose</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span></h2>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Beethoven_Monument,_Bonn" title="Beethoven Monument, Bonn">Beethoven Monument, Bonn</a>, was unveiled in August 1845, in honour of his 75th anniversary. It was the first statue of a composer created in Germany, and the music festival that accompanied the unveiling was the impetus for the very hasty construction of the original <a href="/wiki/Beethovenhalle" title="Beethovenhalle">Beethovenhalle</a> in Bonn (it was designed and built within less than a month, on the urging of <a href="/wiki/Franz_Liszt" title="Franz Liszt">Franz Liszt</a>). A statue to Mozart had been unveiled in <a href="/wiki/Salzburg" title="Salzburg">Salzburg</a>, Austria in 1842. Vienna did not honour Beethoven with a statue until 1880.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> His is the only name inscribed on one of the plaques that trim <a href="/wiki/Symphony_Hall,_Boston" title="Symphony Hall, Boston">Symphony Hall, Boston</a>; the others were left empty because it was felt that only Beethoven's popularity would endure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup></p>
<p>There is a museum, the <a href="/wiki/Beethoven_House" title="Beethoven House">Beethoven House</a>, the place of his birth, in central Bonn. The same city has hosted a musical festival, the <a href="/wiki/Beethovenfest" title="Beethovenfest">Beethovenfest</a>, since 1845. The festival was initially irregular but has been organised annually since 2007.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Ira_F._Brilliant_Center_for_Beethoven_Studies" title="Ira F. Brilliant Center for Beethoven Studies">Ira F. Brilliant Center for Beethoven Studies</a> serves as a museum, research center, and host of lectures and performances devoted solely to this life and works.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Beethoven_(crater)" title="Beethoven (crater)">third largest crater</a> on Mercury is named in his honour, as is the main-belt asteroid <a href="/wiki/1815_Beethoven" title="1815 Beethoven">1815 Beethoven</a>.</p>

<li id="cite_note-landrecht-79"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-landrecht_79-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-landrecht_79-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">On 18 December 1818, the Landrechte, the Austrian court for the nobility, handed over the whole matter of guardianship to the Vienna Magistrate, the court for commoners.
